       , was louder than Concorde at subsonic speeds and during take-off and landing.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">
        <a href="#cite_note-161">
         [156]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Scheduled service from Paris and London to New York's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JFK_International_Airport" title="JFK International Airport">
        John F. Kennedy Airport
       </a>
       began on 22 November 1977.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">
        <a href="#cite_note-162">
         [157]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1977, British Airways and
       <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">
        Singapore Airlines
       </a>
       shared a Concorde for flights between London and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Singapore_International_Airport" title="Singapore International Airport">
        Singapore International Airport
       </a>
       at Paya Lebar via Bahrain. The aircraft, BA's Concorde G-BOAD, was painted in Singapore Airlines livery on the port side and British Airways livery on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Starboard" title="Starboard">
        starboard
       </a>
       side.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
        <a href="#cite_note-163">
         [158]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-singaconc_164-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-singaconc-164">
         [159]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The service was discontinued after three return flights because of noise complaints from the Malaysian government;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165">
        <a href="#cite_note-165">
         [160]
        </a>
       </sup>
       it could only be reinstated on a new route bypassing Malaysian airspace in 1979. A dispute with India prevented Concorde from reaching supersonic speeds in Indian airspace, so the route was eventually declared not viable and discontinued in 1980.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
        <a href="#cite_note-166">
         [161]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During the
       <a href="/wiki/Mexican_oil_boom" title="Mexican oil boom">
        Mexican oil boom
       </a>
       , Air France flew Concorde twice weekly to Mexico City's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benito_Ju%C3%A1rez_International_Airport" title="Benito Juárez International Airport">
        Benito Juárez International Airport
       </a>
       via Washington, DC, or New York City, from September 1978 to November 1982.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167">
        <a href="#cite_note-167">
         [162]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
        <a href="#cite_note-168">
         [163]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The worldwide economic crisis during that period resulted in this route's cancellation; the last flights were almost empty. The routing between Washington or New York and Mexico City included a deceleration, from Mach 2.02 to Mach 0.95, to cross Florida subsonically and avoid creating a sonic boom over the state; Concorde then re-accelerated back to high speed while crossing the Gulf of Mexico. On 1 April 1989, on an around-the-world luxury tour charter, British Airways implemented changes to this routing that allowed G-BOAF to maintain Mach 2.02 by passing around Florida to the east and south. Periodically Concorde visited the region on similar chartered flights to Mexico City and Acapulco.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">
        <a href="#cite_note-169">
         [164]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       From December 1978 to May 1980,
       <a href="/wiki/Braniff_International_Airways" title="Braniff International Airways">
        Braniff International Airways
       </a>
       leased 11 Concordes, five from Air France and six from British Airways.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">
        <a href="#cite_note-170">
         [165]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These were used on subsonic flights between
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dallas-Fort_Worth_International_Airport" title="Dallas-Fort Worth International Airport">
        Dallas-Fort Worth
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Dulles_International_Airport" title="Washington Dulles International Airport">
        Washington Dulles International Airport
       </a>
       , flown by Braniff flight crews.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171">
        <a href="#cite_note-171">
         [166]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Air France and British Airways crews then took over for the continuing supersonic flights to London and Paris.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172">
        <a href="#cite_note-172">
         [167]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The aircraft were registered in both the United States and their home countries; the European registration was covered while being operated by Braniff, retaining full AF/BA liveries. The flights were not profitable and typically less than 50% booked, forcing Braniff to end its tenure as the only US Concorde operator in May 1980.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-braniconc_173-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-braniconc-173">
         [168]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174">
        <a href="#cite_note-174">
         [169]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In its early years, the British Airways Concorde service had a greater number of "no shows" (passengers who booked a flight and then failed to appear at the gate for boarding) than any other aircraft in the fleet.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175">
        <a href="#cite_note-175">
         [170]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="British_Caledonian_interest">
        British Caledonian interest
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: British Caledonian interest">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Following the launch of British Airways Concorde services, Britain's other major airline,
       <a href="/wiki/British_Caledonian" title="British Caledonian">
        British Caledonian
       </a>
       (BCal), set up a task force headed by Gordon Davidson, BA's former Concorde director, to investigate the possibility of their own Concorde operations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176">
        <a href="#cite_note-176">
         [171]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177">
        <a href="#cite_note-177">
         [172]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178">
        <a href="#cite_note-178">
         [173]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This was seen as particularly viable for the airline's long-haul network as there were two unsold aircraft then available for purchase.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whitetails_179-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-whitetails-179">
         [174]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Concorde_details_180-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Concorde_details-180">
         [175]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-final_SST_181-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-final_SST-181">
         [176]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       One important reason for BCal's interest in Concorde was that the
       <a href="/wiki/British_Caledonian_in_the_1970s#Spheres_of_influence" title="British Caledonian in the 1970s">
        British Government's 1976 aviation policy review
       </a>
       had opened the possibility of BA setting up supersonic services in competition with BCal's established sphere of influence. To counteract this potential threat, BCal considered their own independent Concorde plans, as well as a partnership with BA.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182">
        <a href="#cite_note-182">
         [177]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cancel_Concorde_183-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cancel_Concorde-183">
         [178]
        </a>
       </sup>
       BCal were considered most likely to have set up a Concorde service on the Gatwick–Lagos route, a major source of revenue and profits within BCal's scheduled route network;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184">
        <a href="#cite_note-184">
         [179]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185">
        <a href="#cite_note-185">
         [180]
        </a>
       </sup>
       BCal's Concorde task force did assess the viability of a daily supersonic service complementing the existing subsonic widebody service on this route.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Concorde_details_180-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Concorde_details-180">
         [175]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cancel_Concorde_183-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-cancel_Concorde-183">
         [178]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BCAL_Concorde_186-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BCAL_Concorde-186">
         [181]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       BCal entered into a bid to acquire at least one Concorde.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whitetails_179-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-whitetails-179">
         [174]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-final_SST_181-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-final_SST-181">
         [176]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BCAL_Concorde_186-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-BCAL_Concorde-186">
         [181]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, BCal eventually arranged for two aircraft to be leased from BA and
       <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9rospatiale" title="Aérospatiale">
        Aérospatiale
       </a>
       respectively, to be maintained by either BA or Air France. BCal's envisaged two-Concorde fleet would have required a high level of aircraft usage to be cost-effective; therefore, BCal had decided to operate the second aircraft on a supersonic service between Gatwick and Atlanta, with a stopover at either Gander or Halifax.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Concorde_details_180-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Concorde_details-180">
         [175]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Consideration was given to services to Houston and various points on its South American network at a later stage.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BCAL_Concorde_186-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-BCAL_Concorde-186">
         [181]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BCal_Package_187-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BCal_Package-187">
         [182]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Both supersonic services were to be launched at some point during 1980; however, steeply rising oil prices caused by the
       <a href="/wiki/1979_energy_crisis" title="1979 energy crisis">
        1979 energy crisis
       </a>
       led to BCal shelving their supersonic ambitions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cancel_Concorde_183-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-cancel_Concorde-183">
         [178]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="British_Airways_buys_its_Concordes_outright">
        British Airways buys its Concordes outright
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: British Airways buys its Concordes outright">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       By around 1981 in the UK, the future for Concorde looked bleak. The British government had lost money operating Concorde every year, and moves were afoot to cancel the service entirely. A cost projection came back with greatly reduced metallurgical testing costs because the test rig for the wings had built up enough data to last for 30 years and could be shut down. Despite this, the government was not keen to continue. In 1983, BA's managing director,
       <a href="/wiki/John_King,_Baron_King_of_Wartnaby" title="John King, Baron King of Wartnaby">
        Sir John King
       </a>
       , convinced the government to sell the aircraft outright to the then
       <a href="/wiki/Nationalization" title="Nationalization">
        state-owned
       </a>
       British Airways for £16.5 million plus the first year's profits.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188">
        <a href="#cite_note-188">
         [183]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-concewhitele_189-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-concewhitele-189">
         [184]
        </a>
       </sup>
       British Airways was subsequently privatized in 1987.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Operating_economics">
        Operating economics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Operating economics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 1984,
       <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" title="Pan American World Airways">
        Pan American
       </a>
       accused the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Government" title="British Government">
        British Government
       </a>
       of subsidising
       <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">
        British Airways
       </a>
       Concorde air fares, on which a return London-New York was £2,399 (£7076 today), compared to £1,986 (£5858) with a subsonic first class return, and London-Washington return was £2,426 (£7156) instead of £2,258 (£6660) subsonic.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190">
        <a href="#cite_note-190">
         [185]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Research revealed that the Concorde passengers thought that the fare was higher than it actually was, so airlines raised ticket prices to match these perceptions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nova_72-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-nova-72">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is reported that British Airways then ran Concorde at a profit, unlike their French counterpart.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191">
        <a href="#cite_note-191">
         [186]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
          <span title="The material near this tag needs to be fact-checked with the cited source(s). (January 2018)">
           verification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192">
        <a href="#cite_note-192">
         [187]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
          <span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (January 2018)">
           not in citation given
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Its estimated operating costs were $3,800 per block hour in 1972, compared to actual 1971 operating costs of $1,835 for a 707 and $3,500 for a 747; for a 3,050 nmi London-New-York sector, a 707 cost $13,750 - $3.04c per set/nmi, a 747 $26,200 - $2.4c per seat/nmi and the Concorde $14,250 - $4.5c per seat/nmi.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193">
        <a href="#cite_note-193">
         [188]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_services">
        Other services
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Other services">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Between March 1984 and March 1991, British Airways flew a thrice-weekly Concorde service between London and Miami, stopping at Washington Dulles International Airport.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194">
        <a href="#cite_note-194">
         [189]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195">
        <a href="#cite_note-195">
         [190]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Until 2003, Air France and British Airways continued to operate the New York services daily. From 1987 to 2003 British Airways flew a Saturday morning Concorde service to
       <a href="/wiki/Grantley_Adams_International_Airport" title="Grantley Adams International Airport">
        Grantley Adams International Airport
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">
        Barbados
       </a>
       , during the summer and winter holiday season.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196">
        <a href="#cite_note-196">
         [191]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197">
        <a href="#cite_note-197">
         [192]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Prior to the
       <a href="/wiki/Air_France_Flight_4590" title="Air France Flight 4590">
        Air France Paris crash
       </a>
       , several UK and French tour operators operated charter flights to European destinations on a regular basis;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198">
        <a href="#cite_note-198">
         [193]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199">
        <a href="#cite_note-199">
         [194]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the charter business was viewed as lucrative by British Airways and Air France.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200">
        <a href="#cite_note-200">
         [195]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1997, British Airways held a promotional contest to mark the 10th anniversary of the airline's move into the private sector. The promotion was a lottery to fly to New York held for 190 tickets valued at £5,400 each, to be offered at £10. Contestants had to call a special hotline to compete with up to 20 million people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201">
        <a href="#cite_note-201">
         [196]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Retirement">
        Retirement
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Retirement">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Concorde_on_Bristol.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="535" data-file-width="750" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Concorde_on_Bristol.jpg/220px-Concorde_on_Bristol.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Concorde_on_Bristol.jpg/330px-Concorde_on_Bristol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Concorde_on_Bristol.jpg/440px-Concorde_on_Bristol.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Concorde_on_Bristol.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Concorde's final flight: G-BOAF from Heathrow to Bristol, on 26 November 2003. The extremely high
         <a href="/wiki/Fineness_ratio" title="Fineness ratio">
          fineness ratio
         </a>
         of the fuselage is evident.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Intrepid_museum_aerial.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3365" data-file-width="2243" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Intrepid_museum_aerial.jpg/220px-Intrepid_museum_aerial.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Intrepid_museum_aerial.jpg/330px-Intrepid_museum_aerial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Intrepid_museum_aerial.jpg/440px-Intrepid_museum_aerial.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Intrepid_museum_aerial.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A Concorde at the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intrepid_Museum" title="Intrepid Museum">
          Intrepid Museum
         </a>
         in New York City
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On 10 April 2003, Air France and British Airways simultaneously announced that they would retire Concorde later that year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202">
        <a href="#cite_note-202">
         [197]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They cited low passenger numbers following the 25 July 2000 crash, the
       <a href="/wiki/Economic_effects_arising_from_the_September_11_attacks" title="Economic effects arising from the September 11 attacks">
        slump in air travel
       </a>
       following the
       <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">
        September 11 attacks
       </a>
       , and rising maintenance costs. Although Concorde was technologically advanced when introduced in the 1970s, 30 years later, its analogue cockpit was outdated. There had been little commercial pressure to upgrade Concorde due to a lack of competing aircraft, unlike other airliners of the same era such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">
        Boeing 747
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203">
        <a href="#cite_note-203">
         [198]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By its retirement, it was the last aircraft in the British Airways fleet that had a
       <a href="/wiki/Flight_engineer" title="Flight engineer">
        flight engineer
       </a>
       ; other aircraft, such as the modernised
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/747-400" title="747-400">
        747-400
       </a>
       , had eliminated the role.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fliengi_204-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-fliengi-204">
         [199]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 11 April 2003,
       <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">
        Virgin Atlantic
       </a>
       founder Sir
       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Branson" title="Richard Branson">
        Richard Branson
       </a>
       announced that the company was interested in purchasing British Airways' Concorde fleet "for the same price that they were given them for -- one pound".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205">
        <a href="#cite_note-205">
         [200]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206">
        <a href="#cite_note-206">
         [201]
        </a>
       </sup>
       British Airways dismissed the idea, prompting Virgin to increase their offer to £1 million each.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207">
        <a href="#cite_note-207">
         [202]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208">
        <a href="#cite_note-208">
         [203]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Branson claimed that when BA was privatised, a clause in the agreement required them to allow another British airline to operate Concorde if BA ceased to do so, but the Government denied the existence of such a clause.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209">
        <a href="#cite_note-209">
         [204]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In October 2003, Branson wrote in
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">
         The Economist
        </a>
       </i>
       that his final offer was "over £5 million" and that he had intended to operate the fleet "for many years to come".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210">
        <a href="#cite_note-210">
         [205]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The chances for keeping Concorde in service were stifled by Airbus's lack of support for continued maintenance.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211">
        <a href="#cite_note-211">
         [206]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212">
        <a href="#cite_note-212">
         [207]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213">
        <a href="#cite_note-213">
         [N 6]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       It has been suggested that Concorde was not withdrawn for the reasons usually given but that it became apparent during the grounding of Concorde that the airlines could make more profit carrying first-class passengers subsonically.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214">
        <a href="#cite_note-214">
         [208]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A lack of commitment to Concorde from Director of Engineering Alan MacDonald was cited as having undermined BA's resolve to continue operating Concorde.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215">
        <a href="#cite_note-215">
         [209]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Air_France">
        Air France
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Air France">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px">
        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ConcordeCDG.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="1314" data-file-width="2396" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/ConcordeCDG.jpg/220px-ConcordeCDG.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/ConcordeCDG.jpg/330px-ConcordeCDG.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/ConcordeCDG.jpg/440px-ConcordeCDG.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          Air France Concorde at
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paris-Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" title="Paris-Charles de Gaulle Airport">
           Paris-Charles de Gaulle Airport
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aerospatial_Concorde_(6018513515).jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Aerospatial_Concorde_%286018513515%29.jpg/220px-Aerospatial_Concorde_%286018513515%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Aerospatial_Concorde_%286018513515%29.jpg/330px-Aerospatial_Concorde_%286018513515%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Aerospatial_Concorde_%286018513515%29.jpg/440px-Aerospatial_Concorde_%286018513515%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          Air France Concorde in
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinsheim_Auto_%26_Technik_Museum" title="Sinsheim Auto &amp; Technik Museum">
           Auto &amp; Technik Museum Sinsheim
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Air France made its final commercial Concorde landing in the United States in New York City from Paris on 30 May 2003.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216">
        <a href="#cite_note-216">
         [210]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217">
        <a href="#cite_note-217">
         [211]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Air France's final Concorde flight took place on 27 June 2003 when F-BVFC retired to Toulouse.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218">
        <a href="#cite_note-218">
         [212]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       An
       <a href="/wiki/Auction" title="Auction">
        auction
       </a>
       of Concorde parts and memorabilia for Air France was held at
       <a href="/wiki/Christie%27s" title="Christie's">
        Christie's
       </a>
       in Paris on 15 November 2003; 1,300 people attended, and several lots exceeded their predicted values.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219">
        <a href="#cite_note-219">
         [213]
        </a>
       </sup>
       French Concorde F-BVFC was retired to Toulouse and kept functional for a short time after the end of service, in case taxi runs were required in support of the French judicial enquiry into the 2000 crash.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220">
        <a href="#cite_note-220">
         [214]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The aircraft is now fully retired and no longer functional.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221">
        <a href="#cite_note-221">
         [215]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       French Concorde F-BTSD has been retired to the "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_de_l%27Air" title="Musée de l'Air">
        Musée de l'Air
       </a>
       " at
       <a href="/wiki/Paris%E2%80%93Le_Bourget_Airport" title="Paris–Le Bourget Airport">
        Paris–Le Bourget Airport
       </a>
       near Paris; unlike the other museum Concordes, a few of the systems are being kept functional. For instance, the famous "droop nose" can still be lowered and raised. This led to rumours that they could be prepared for future flights for special occasions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vafhtk_222-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-vafhtk-222">
         [216]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Concorde_F-BVFA.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3216" data-file-width="4288" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Concorde_F-BVFA.JPG/220px-Concorde_F-BVFA.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Concorde_F-BVFA.JPG/330px-Concorde_F-BVFA.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Concorde_F-BVFA.JPG/440px-Concorde_F-BVFA.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Concorde_F-BVFA.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Air France Concorde on display at
         <a href="/wiki/Steven_F._Udvar-Hazy_Center" title="Steven F. Udvar-Hazy Center">
          Steven F. Udvar-Hazy Center
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       French Concorde F-BVFB currently rests at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinsheim_Auto_%26_Technik_Museum" title="Sinsheim Auto &amp; Technik Museum">
        Auto &amp; Technik Museum Sinsheim
       </a>
       at
       <a href="/wiki/Sinsheim" title="Sinsheim">
        Sinsheim
       </a>
       , Germany, after its last flight from Paris to Baden-Baden, followed by a spectacular transport to
       <a href="/wiki/Sinsheim" title="Sinsheim">
        Sinsheim
       </a>
       via barge and road. The museum also has a
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-144" title="Tupolev Tu-144">
        Tupolev Tu-144
       </a>
       on display – this is the only place where both supersonic airliners can be seen together.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223">
        <a href="#cite_note-223">
         [217]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1989, Air France signed a letter of agreement to donate a Concorde to the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Air_and_Space_Museum" title="National Air and Space Museum">
        National Air and Space Museum
       </a>
       in Washington D.C. upon the aircraft's retirement. On 12 June 2003, Air France honoured that agreement, donating Concorde F-BVFA (serial 205) to the Museum upon the completion of its last flight. This aircraft was the first Air France Concorde to open service to Rio de Janeiro, Washington, D.C., and New York and had flown 17,824 hours. It is on display at the Smithsonian's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steven_F._Udvar-Hazy" title="Steven F. Udvar-Hazy">
        Steven F. Udvar-Hazy
       </a>
       Center at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dulles_Airport" title="Dulles Airport">
        Dulles Airport
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224">
        <a href="#cite_note-224">
         [218]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="British_Airways">
        British Airways
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: British Airways">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:G-BOAB_in_new_home_(8472694454).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/G-BOAB_in_new_home_%288472694454%29.jpg/220px-G-BOAB_in_new_home_%288472694454%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/G-BOAB_in_new_home_%288472694454%29.jpg/330px-G-BOAB_in_new_home_%288472694454%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/G-BOAB_in_new_home_%288472694454%29.jpg/440px-G-BOAB_in_new_home_%288472694454%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:G-BOAB_in_new_home_(8472694454).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         BA Concorde G-BOAB in storage at
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" title="London Heathrow Airport">
          London Heathrow Airport
         </a>
         . This aircraft flew for 22,296 hours between its first flight in 1976 and its final flight in 2000.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       British Airways conducted a North American farewell tour in October 2003. G-BOAG visited
       <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Pearson_International_Airport" title="Toronto Pearson International Airport">
        Toronto Pearson International Airport
       </a>
       on 1 October, after which it flew to New York's John F. Kennedy International Airport.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225">
        <a href="#cite_note-225">
         [219]
        </a>
       </sup>
       G-BOAD visited
       <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">
        Boston
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Logan_International_Airport" title="Logan International Airport">
        Logan International Airport
       </a>
       on 8 October, and G-BOAG visited
       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Dulles_International_Airport" title="Washington Dulles International Airport">
        Washington Dulles International Airport
       </a>
       on 14 October.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226">
        <a href="#cite_note-226">
         [220]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In a week of farewell flights around the United Kingdom, Concorde visited
       <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">
        Birmingham
       </a>
       on 20 October,
       <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">
        Belfast
       </a>
       on 21 October,
       <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">
        Manchester
       </a>
       on 22 October,
       <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">
        Cardiff
       </a>
       on 23 October, and
       <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">
        Edinburgh
       </a>
       on 24 October. Each day the aircraft made a return flight out and back into Heathrow to the cities, often overflying them at low altitude.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227">
        <a href="#cite_note-227">
         [221]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228">
        <a href="#cite_note-228">
         [222]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229">
        <a href="#cite_note-229">
         [223]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 22 October, both Concorde flight BA9021C, a special from Manchester, and BA002 from New York landed simultaneously on both of Heathrow's runways. On 23 October 2003, the Queen consented to the illumination of
       <a href="/wiki/Windsor_Castle" title="Windsor Castle">
        Windsor Castle
       </a>
       , an honour reserved for state events and visiting dignitaries, as Concorde's last west-bound commercial flight departed London.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230">
        <a href="#cite_note-230">
         [224]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">
        British Airways
       </a>
       retired its Concorde fleet on 24 October 2003.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jlfin_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-jlfin-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       G-BOAG left New York to a fanfare similar to that given for Air France's F-BTSD, while two more made round trips, G-BOAF over the
       <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Biscay" title="Bay of Biscay">
        Bay of Biscay
       </a>
       , carrying VIP guests including former Concorde pilots, and G-BOAE to Edinburgh. The three aircraft then circled over London, having received special permission to fly at low altitude, before landing in sequence at Heathrow. The captain of the New York to London flight was Mike Bannister.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231">
        <a href="#cite_note-231">
         [225]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The final flight of a Concorde in the US occurred on 5 November 2003 when G-BOAG flew from New York's JFK Airport to Seattle's
       <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Field" title="Boeing Field">
        Boeing Field
       </a>
       to join the
       <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Flight" title="Museum of Flight">
        Museum of Flight
       </a>
       's permanent collection. The plane was piloted by Mike Bannister and Les Broadie, who claimed a flight time of three hours, 55 minutes and 12 seconds, a record between the two cities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232">
        <a href="#cite_note-232">
         [226]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The museum had been pursuing a Concorde for their collection since 1984.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233">
        <a href="#cite_note-233">
         [227]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The final flight of a Concorde worldwide took place on 26 November 2003 with a landing at Filton, Bristol, UK.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234">
        <a href="#cite_note-234">
         [228]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       All of BA's Concorde fleet have been grounded, drained of hydraulic fluid and their airworthiness certificates withdrawn. Jock Lowe, ex-chief Concorde pilot and manager of the fleet estimated in 2004 that it would cost £10–15 million to make G-BOAF airworthy again.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vafhtk_222-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-vafhtk-222">
         [216]
        </a>
       </sup>
       BA maintain ownership and have stated that they will not fly again due to a lack of support from Airbus.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235">
        <a href="#cite_note-235">
         [229]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 1 December 2003,
       <a href="/wiki/Bonhams" title="Bonhams">
        Bonhams
       </a>
       held an auction of British Airways Concorde artefacts, including a nose cone, at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympia_Exhibition_Centre" title="Olympia Exhibition Centre">
        Kensington Olympia
       </a>
       in London.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236">
        <a href="#cite_note-236">
         [230]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237">
        <a href="#cite_note-237">
         [231]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Proceeds of around £750,000 were raised, with the majority going to charity. G-BOAD is currently on display at the
       <a href="/wiki/Intrepid_Sea,_Air_%26_Space_Museum" title="Intrepid Sea, Air &amp; Space Museum">
        Intrepid Sea, Air &amp; Space Museum
       </a>
       in New York.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-intrepid_238-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-intrepid-238">
         [232]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2007, BA announced that the advertising spot at Heathrow where a 40% scale model of Concorde was located would not be retained; the model is now on display at the
       <a href="/wiki/Brooklands_Museum" title="Brooklands Museum">
        Brooklands Museum
       </a>
       , in Surrey, England.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239">
        <a href="#cite_note-239">
         [233]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Restoration">
        Restoration
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Restoration">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Although only used for spares after being retired from test flying and trials work in 1981, Concorde G-BBDG was dismantled and transported by road from
       <a href="/wiki/Filton" title="Filton">
        Filton
       </a>
       then restored from essentially a shell at the
       <a href="/wiki/Brooklands_Museum" title="Brooklands Museum">
        Brooklands Museum
       </a>
       in Surrey,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240">
        <a href="#cite_note-240">
         [234]
        </a>
       </sup>
       where it remains open to visitors to the museum.
      </p>
      <p>
       One of the youngest Concordes (F-BTSD) is on display at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_de_l%27Air" title="Musée de l'Air">
        Le Bourget Air and Space Museum
       </a>
       in Paris. In February 2010, it was announced that the museum and a group of volunteer Air France technicians intend to restore F-BTSD so it can taxi under its own power.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241">
        <a href="#cite_note-241">
         [235]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In May 2010, it was reported that the British Save Concorde Group and French Olympus 593 groups had begun inspecting the engines of a Concorde at the French museum; their intent is to restore the airliner to a condition where it can fly in demonstrations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242">
        <a href="#cite_note-242">
         [236]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Save Concorde Group hoped to get F-BTSD flying for the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012_London_Olympics" title="2012 London Olympics">
        2012 London Olympics
       </a>
       , but this never happened. The work for restoring F-BTSD to operating condition as of September 2015 is currently not very well known, and it is still being housed in Le Bourget as a museum exhibit. In 2015, the organisation Club Concorde announced that it had raised funds of £120 million for a static display
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243">
        <a href="#cite_note-243">
         [237]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and to buy the Concorde at Le Bourget, restore it and return it to service as a heritage aircraft for air displays and charter hire by 2019, to coincide with the 50th anniversary of Concorde's first flight.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardianbreakthrough_244-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-guardianbreakthrough-244">
         [238]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In July 2015, it was reported that planning permission had been granted for the construction of the museum at
       <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Filton_Airport" title="Bristol Filton Airport">
        Bristol Filton Airport
       </a>
       to house G-BOAF the last Concorde where it is intended to form a key exhibit of the new
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bristol_Aviation_Heritage_Museum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bristol Aviation Heritage Museum (page does not exist)">
        Bristol Aviation Heritage Museum
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245">
        <a href="#cite_note-245">
         [239]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_service_plan">
        Return to service plan
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Return to service plan">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In September 2015, Club Concorde announced it had secured over £160 million to return an aircraft to service.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246">
        <a href="#cite_note-246">
         [240]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Club Concorde president Paul James said:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247">
        <a href="#cite_note-247">
         [241]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        The main obstacle to any Concorde project to date has been "Where's the money?"—a question we heard ad nauseam, until we found an investor. Now that money is no longer the problem it's over to those who can help us make it happen.
       </p>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       The organisation aims to buy the Concorde currently on display at Le Bourget airport. A tentative date of 2019 has been put forward for the return to flight—50 years after its maiden journey.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardianbreakthrough_244-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-guardianbreakthrough-244">
         [238]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, due to regulatory and technical hurdles, some of the aviation community are highly skeptical of the plan, including former Concorde captain and Club Concorde co-founder William "Jock" Lowe, who was quoted in June 2016 saying:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248">
        <a href="#cite_note-248">
         [242]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        Let's assume you could rip the whole thing apart and ultrasound the fuselage. There are thousands, many thousands of hydraulic seals on the airplane. … Every one of them would have to be remanufactured and replaced. [But] the manufacturing facilities are just not there. … And if you got them all together, what sort of testing regimen would be there? … It took seven years of flight testing to get it into service in the first place.
       </p>
      </blockquote>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Operators">
        Operators
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Operators">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">
         Air France
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">
         British Airways
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Braniff_International_Airways#Concorde_SST" title="Braniff International Airways">
         Braniff International Airways
        </a>
        (1 on short term lease)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-braniconc_173-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-braniconc-173">
          [168]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">
         Singapore Airlines
        </a>
        (1 on short term
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wet_lease" title="Wet lease">
         wet lease
        </a>
        )
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-singaconc_164-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-singaconc-164">
          [159]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">
        Accidents and incidents
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Air_France_Flight_4590">
        Air France Flight 4590
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Air France Flight 4590">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Air_France_Flight_4590" title="Air France Flight 4590">
        Air France Flight 4590
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Concorde_Air_France_Flight_4590_fire_on_runway.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="194" data-file-width="310" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Concorde_Air_France_Flight_4590_fire_on_runway.jpg/220px-Concorde_Air_France_Flight_4590_fire_on_runway.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/0/03/Concorde_Air_France_Flight_4590_fire_on_runway.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Concorde_Air_France_Flight_4590_fire_on_runway.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Flight 4590 during takeoff
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On 25 July 2000, Air France Flight 4590, registration F-BTSC,
       <a href="/wiki/Air_France_Flight_4590" title="Air France Flight 4590">
        crashed
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Gonesse" title="Gonesse">
        Gonesse
       </a>
       , France after departing from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paris-Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Paris-Charles de Gaulle">
        Paris-Charles de Gaulle
       </a>
       en route to
       <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">
        John F. Kennedy International Airport
       </a>
       in New York City, killing all 100 passengers and 9 crew members on board the flight, and 4 people on the ground. It was the only fatal accident involving Concorde.
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the official investigation conducted by the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Bureau_d%27Enqu%C3%AAtes_et_d%27Analyses_pour_la_S%C3%A9curit%C3%A9_de_l%27Aviation_Civile" title="Bureau d'Enquêtes et d'Analyses pour la Sécurité de l'Aviation Civile">
         Bureau d'Enquêtes et d'Analyses pour la Sécurité de l'Aviation Civile
        </a>
       </i>
       (BEA), the crash was caused by a metallic strip that had fallen from a
       <a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines" title="Continental Airlines">
        Continental Airlines
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10" title="McDonnell Douglas DC-10">
        DC-10
       </a>
       that had taken off minutes earlier. This fragment punctured a tyre on Concorde's left main wheel bogie during take-off. The tyre exploded, and a piece of rubber hit the fuel tank, which caused a fuel leak and led to a fire. The crew shut down engine number 2 in response to a fire warning, and with engine number 1 surging and producing little power, the aircraft was unable to gain altitude or speed. The aircraft entered a rapid pitch-up then a violent descent, rolling left and crashing tail-low into the Hôtelissimo Les Relais Bleus Hotel in Gonesse.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEndres2001110–113_249-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEndres2001110–113-249">
         [243]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The claim that a metallic strip caused the crash was disputed during the trial both by witnesses (including the pilot of
       <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Chirac" title="Jacques Chirac">
        Jacques Chirac
       </a>
       's aircraft that had just landed on an adjacent runway when Flight 4590 caught fire) and by an independent French TV investigation that found a wheel spacer had not been installed in the left-side main gear and that the plane caught fire some 1,000 feet from where the metallic strip lay.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250">
        <a href="#cite_note-250">
         [244]
        </a>
       </sup>
       British investigators and former French Concorde pilots looked at several other possibilities that the BEA report ignored, including an unbalanced weight distribution in the fuel tanks and loose landing gear. They came to the conclusion that the Concorde veered off course on the runway, which reduced takeoff speed below the crucial minimum. John Hutchinson, who had served as a Concorde captain for 15 years with British Airways, said that "the fire on its own should have been 'eminently survivable; the pilot should have been able to fly his way out of trouble'", had it not been for a "lethal combination of operational error and 'negligence' by the maintenance department of Air France" that "nobody wants to talk about".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Observer_251-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Observer-251">
         [245]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252">
        <a href="#cite_note-252">
         [246]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253">
        <a href="#cite_note-253">
         [247]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 6 December 2010, Continental Airlines and John Taylor, one of its mechanics, were found guilty of involuntary manslaughter,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254">
        <a href="#cite_note-254">
         [248]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but on 30 November 2012, a French court overturned the conviction, saying mistakes by Continental and Taylor did not make them criminally responsible.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-conviction_overturned_255-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-conviction_overturned-255">
         [249]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Prior to the accident, Concorde had been arguably the safest operational passenger airliner in the world in passenger deaths-per-kilometres travelled with zero, but there had been two prior non-fatal accidents and a rate of tyre damage some 30 times higher than subsonic airliners from 1995 to 2000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AAIB89_256-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AAIB89-256">
         [250]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AAIB93_257-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AAIB93-257">
         [251]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258">
        <a href="#cite_note-258">
         [252]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259">
        <a href="#cite_note-259">
         [253]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Safety improvements were made in the wake of the crash, including more secure electrical controls,
       <a href="/wiki/Kevlar" title="Kevlar">
        Kevlar
       </a>
       lining on the fuel tanks and specially developed burst-resistant tyres.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260">
        <a href="#cite_note-260">
         [254]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first flight with the modifications departed from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_airport" title="London Heathrow airport">
        London Heathrow
       </a>
       on 17 July 2001, piloted by BA Chief Concorde Pilot
       <a href="/wiki/Mike_Bannister" title="Mike Bannister">
        Mike Bannister
       </a>
       . During the 3-hour 20-minute flight over the mid-Atlantic towards Iceland, Bannister attained Mach 2.02 and 60,000 ft (18,000 m) before returning to
       <a href="/wiki/RAF_Brize_Norton" title="RAF Brize Norton">
        RAF Brize Norton
       </a>
       . The test flight, intended to resemble the London–New York route, was declared a success and was watched on live TV, and by crowds on the ground at both locations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261">
        <a href="#cite_note-261">
         [255]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The first flight with passengers after the accident took place on 11 September 2001, landing shortly before the
       <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">
        World Trade Center attacks
       </a>
       in the United States. This was not a commercial flight: all the passengers were BA employees.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262">
        <a href="#cite_note-262">
         [256]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Normal commercial operations resumed on 7 November 2001 by BA and AF (aircraft G-BOAE and F-BTSD), with service to New York JFK, where mayor
       <a href="/wiki/Rudy_Giuliani" title="Rudy Giuliani">
        Rudy Giuliani
       </a>
       greeted the passengers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263">
        <a href="#cite_note-263">
         [257]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264">
        <a href="#cite_note-264">
         [258]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_accidents_and_incidents">
        Other accidents and incidents
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Other accidents and incidents">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:G-BOAF_rudder_damage.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="963" data-file-width="1699" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/G-BOAF_rudder_damage.jpg/220px-G-BOAF_rudder_damage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/G-BOAF_rudder_damage.jpg/330px-G-BOAF_rudder_damage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/G-BOAF_rudder_damage.jpg/440px-G-BOAF_rudder_damage.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:G-BOAF_rudder_damage.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Damage to Concorde rudder after 1989 accident
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Concorde had suffered two previous non-fatal accidents that were similar to each other.
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        12 April 1989: A Concorde of British registration, G-BOAF, on a chartered flight from
        <a href="/wiki/Christchurch" title="Christchurch">
         Christchurch
        </a>
        , New Zealand, to Sydney, suffered a structural failure in-flight at supersonic speed. As the aircraft was climbing and accelerating through Mach 1.7 a "thud" was heard. The crew did not notice any handling problems, and they assumed the thud they heard was a minor
        <a href="/wiki/Compressor_stall" title="Compressor stall">
         engine surge
        </a>
        . No further difficulty was encountered until descent through 40,000 feet at Mach 1.3, when a vibration was felt throughout the aircraft, lasting two to three minutes. Most of the upper rudder had become separated from the aircraft at this point. Aircraft handling was unaffected, and the aircraft made a safe landing at Sydney. The UK's
        <a href="/wiki/Air_Accidents_Investigation_Branch" title="Air Accidents Investigation Branch">
         Air Accidents Investigation Branch
        </a>
        (AAIB) concluded that the skin of the rudder had been separating from the rudder structure over a period of time before the accident due to moisture seepage past the
        <a href="/wiki/Rivet" title="Rivet">
         rivets
        </a>
        in the rudder. Furthermore, production staff had not followed proper procedures during an earlier modification of the rudder, but the procedures were difficult to adhere to.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AAIB89_256-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-AAIB89-256">
          [250]
         </a>
        </sup>
        The aircraft was repaired and returned to service.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AAIB89_256-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-AAIB89-256">
          [250]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        21 March 1992: A Concorde of British registration, G-BOAB, on a scheduled flight from London to New York, also suffered a structural failure in-flight at supersonic speed. While cruising at Mach 2, at approximately 53,000 feet above mean sea level, the crew heard a "thump". No difficulties in handling were noticed, and no instruments gave any irregular indications. This crew also suspected there had been a minor engine surge. One hour later, during descent and while decelerating below Mach 1.4, a sudden "severe" vibration began throughout the aircraft.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AAIB93_257-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-AAIB93-257">
          [251]
         </a>
        </sup>
        The vibration worsened when power was added to the No 2 engine, and it was attenuated when that engine's power was reduced. The crew shut down the No 2 engine and made a successful landing in New York, noting only that increased rudder control was needed to keep the aircraft on its intended approach course. Again, the skin had become separated from the structure of the rudder, which led to most of the upper rudder becoming separated in-flight. The (AAIB) concluded that repair materials had leaked into the structure of the rudder during a recent repair, weakening the bond between the skin and the structure of the rudder, leading to it breaking up in-flight. The large size of the repair had made it difficult to keep repair materials out of the structure, and prior to this accident, the severity of the effect of these repair materials on the structure and skin of the rudder was not appreciated.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AAIB93_257-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-AAIB93-257">
          [251]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        The 2010 trial involving
        <a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines" title="Continental Airlines">
         Continental Airlines
        </a>
        over the crash of Flight 4590 established that from 1976 until Flight 4590 there had been 57 tyre failures involving Concordes during takeoffs, including a near-crash at
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dulles_Airport" title="Dulles Airport">
         Dulles Airport
        </a>
        on 14 June 1979 involving Air France Flight 54 where a tyre blowout pierced the plane's fuel tank and damaged the port-side engine and electrical cables, with the loss of two of the craft's hydraulic systems.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265">
         <a href="#cite_note-265">
          [259]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Aircraft_on_display">
        Aircraft on display
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Aircraft on display">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Concorde_aircraft_histories" title="Concorde aircraft histories">
        Concorde aircraft histories
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Of the twenty aircraft built, 18 are still complete. Many are on display at museums in the United Kingdom, France, the United States, Germany and Barbados.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Comparable_aircraft">
        Comparable aircraft
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Comparable aircraft">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tu-144">
        Tu-144
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Tu-144">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Russian_Tu-144LL_SST_Flying_Laboratory_Takeoff_at_Zhukovsky_Air_Development_Center.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2363" data-file-width="3000" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Russian_Tu-144LL_SST_Flying_Laboratory_Takeoff_at_Zhukovsky_Air_Development_Center.jpg/220px-Russian_Tu-144LL_SST_Flying_Laboratory_Takeoff_at_Zhukovsky_Air_Development_Center.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Russian_Tu-144LL_SST_Flying_Laboratory_Takeoff_at_Zhukovsky_Air_Development_Center.jpg/330px-Russian_Tu-144LL_SST_Flying_Laboratory_Takeoff_at_Zhukovsky_Air_Development_Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Russian_Tu-144LL_SST_Flying_Laboratory_Takeoff_at_Zhukovsky_Air_Development_Center.jpg/440px-Russian_Tu-144LL_SST_Flying_Laboratory_Takeoff_at_Zhukovsky_Air_Development_Center.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Russian_Tu-144LL_SST_Flying_Laboratory_Takeoff_at_Zhukovsky_Air_Development_Center.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Tu-144FL as a research aircraft for
         <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">
          NASA
         </a>
         in 1997
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sinsheim_Auto_%26_Technik_Museum.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Sinsheim_Auto_%26_Technik_Museum.jpg/220px-Sinsheim_Auto_%26_Technik_Museum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Sinsheim_Auto_%26_Technik_Museum.jpg/330px-Sinsheim_Auto_%26_Technik_Museum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Sinsheim_Auto_%26_Technik_Museum.jpg/440px-Sinsheim_Auto_%26_Technik_Museum.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sinsheim_Auto_%26_Technik_Museum.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Concorde (left) and Tu-144 in
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sinsheim_Auto_%26_Technik_Museum" title="Sinsheim Auto &amp; Technik Museum">
          Auto &amp; Technik Museum Sinsheim
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The only supersonic airliner in direct competition with Concorde was the Soviet
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-144" title="Tupolev Tu-144">
        Tupolev Tu-144
       </a>
       , nicknamed "Concordski" by Western European journalists for its outward similarity to Concorde.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266">
        <a href="#cite_note-266">
         [260]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It had been alleged that Soviet espionage efforts had resulted in the theft of Concorde blueprints, supposedly to assist in the design of the Tu-144.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267">
        <a href="#cite_note-267">
         [261]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As a result of a rushed development programme, the first Tu-144 prototype was substantially different from the preproduction machines, but both were cruder than Concorde. The Tu-144
       <i>
        S
       </i>
       had a significantly shorter range than Concorde. Jean Rech, Sud Aviation, attributed this to two things,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268">
        <a href="#cite_note-268">
         [262]
        </a>
       </sup>
       a very heavy powerplant with an intake twice as long as that on Concorde, and
       <a href="/wiki/Turbofan#Low-bypass_turbofan" title="Turbofan">
        low-bypass turbofan engines
       </a>
       with too-high a bypass ratio which needed afterburning for cruise. The aircraft had poor control at low speeds because of a simpler supersonic wing design; in addition the Tu-144 required
       <a href="/wiki/Drogue_parachute" title="Drogue parachute">
        braking parachutes
       </a>
       to land while Concorde used anti-lock brakes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269">
        <a href="#cite_note-269">
         [263]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Tu-144 had two crashes, one at the
       <a href="/wiki/1973_Paris_Air_Show_crash" title="1973 Paris Air Show crash">
        1973 Paris Air Show
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270">
        <a href="#cite_note-270">
         [264]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271">
        <a href="#cite_note-271">
         [265]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and another during a pre-delivery test flight in May 1978.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272">
        <a href="#cite_note-272">
         [266]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273">
        <a href="#cite_note-273">
         [267]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Later production Tu-144 versions were more refined and competitive. They had retractable
       <a href="/wiki/Canard_(aeronautics)" title="Canard (aeronautics)">
        canards
       </a>
       for better low-speed control, turbojet engines providing nearly the fuel efficiency and range of Concorde
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rus144_274-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-rus144-274">
         [268]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and a top speed of Mach 2.35. Passenger service commenced in November 1977, but after the 1978 crash the aircraft was taken out of service. The aircraft had an inherently unsafe structural design as a consequence of an automated production method chosen to simplify and speed up manufacturing.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fridlyander_275-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Fridlyander-275">
         [269]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="SST_and_others">
        SST and others
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: SST and others">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Supersonic_transport" title="Supersonic transport">
        Supersonic transport
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The American designs, the "SST" project (for Supersonic Transport) were the
       <a href="/wiki/Boeing_2707" title="Boeing 2707">
        Boeing 2707
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_L-2000" title="Lockheed L-2000">
        Lockheed L-2000
       </a>
       . These were to have been larger, with seating for up to 300 people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276">
        <a href="#cite_note-276">
         [270]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinchester2005a84_277-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinchester2005a84-277">
         [271]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Running a few years behind Concorde, the Boeing 2707 was redesigned to a cropped delta layout; the extra cost of these changes helped to kill the project.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278">
        <a href="#cite_note-278">
         [272]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The operation of US military aircraft such as the Mach 3+
       <a href="/wiki/North_American_XB-70_Valkyrie" title="North American XB-70 Valkyrie">
        North American XB-70 Valkyrie
       </a>
       prototypes and
       <a href="/wiki/Convair_B-58_Hustler" title="Convair B-58 Hustler">
        Convair B-58 Hustler
       </a>
       strategic nuclear bomber had shown that sonic booms were quite capable of reaching the ground,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279">
        <a href="#cite_note-279">
         [273]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the experience from the
       <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_City_sonic_boom_tests" title="Oklahoma City sonic boom tests">
        Oklahoma City sonic boom tests
       </a>
       led to the same environmental concerns that hindered the commercial success of Concorde. The American government cancelled its SST project in 1971, after having spent more than $1 billion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280">
        <a href="#cite_note-280">
         [274]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The only other large supersonic aircraft comparable to Concorde are
       <a href="/wiki/Strategic_bomber" title="Strategic bomber">
        strategic bombers
       </a>
       , principally the Russian
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-22" title="Tupolev Tu-22">
        Tu-22
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-22M" title="Tupolev Tu-22M">
        Tu-22M
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Myasishchev_M-50" title="Myasishchev M-50">
        M-50
       </a>
       (experimental),
       <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_T-4" title="Sukhoi T-4">
        T-4
       </a>
       (experimental),
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-160" title="Tupolev Tu-160">
        Tu-160
       </a>
       and the American XB-70 (experimental) and
       <a href="/wiki/Rockwell_B-1_Lancer" title="Rockwell B-1 Lancer">
        B-1
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281">
        <a href="#cite_note-281">
         [275]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">
        Impact
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Impact">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental">
        Environmental
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Environmental">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Before Concorde's flight trials, developments in the civil aviation industry were largely accepted by governments and their respective electorates. Opposition to Concorde's noise, particularly on the east coast of the United States,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282">
        <a href="#cite_note-282">
