         [276]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283">
        <a href="#cite_note-283">
         [277]
        </a>
       </sup>
       forged a new political agenda on both sides of the Atlantic, with scientists and technology experts across a multitude of industries beginning to take the environmental and social impact more seriously.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284">
        <a href="#cite_note-284">
         [278]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285">
        <a href="#cite_note-285">
         [279]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Although Concorde led directly to the introduction of a general noise abatement programme for aircraft flying out of John F. Kennedy Airport, many found that Concorde was quieter than expected,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nova_72-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-nova-72">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       partly due to the pilots temporarily throttling back their engines to reduce noise during overflight of residential areas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEndres200190_286-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEndres200190-286">
         [280]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Even before commercial flights started, it had been claimed that Concorde was quieter than many other aircraft.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287">
        <a href="#cite_note-287">
         [281]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1971, BAC's technical director was quoted as saying, "It is certain on present evidence and calculations that in the airport context, production Concordes will be no worse than aircraft now in service and will in fact be better than many of them."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288">
        <a href="#cite_note-288">
         [282]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Concorde produced nitrogen oxides in its exhaust, which, despite complicated interactions with other ozone-depleting chemicals, are understood to result in degradation to the
       <a href="/wiki/Ozone_layer" title="Ozone layer">
        ozone layer
       </a>
       at the
       <a href="/wiki/Stratosphere" title="Stratosphere">
        stratospheric
       </a>
       altitudes it cruised.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-emissions_289-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-emissions-289">
         [283]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It has been pointed out that other, lower-flying, airliners produce ozone during their flights in the troposphere, but vertical transit of gases between the layers is restricted. The small fleet meant overall ozone-layer degradation caused by Concorde was negligible.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-emissions_289-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-emissions-289">
         [283]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1995, David Fahey, of the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">
        National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration
       </a>
       in the United States, warned that a fleet of 500 supersonic aircraft with exhausts similar to Concorde might produce in a 2 per cent drop in global ozone levels, much higher than previously thought. Each 1 per cent drop in ozone is estimated to increase the incidence of non-melanoma skin cancer worldwide by 2 per cent. Dr Fahey said if these particles are produced by highly oxidised sulphur in the fuel, as he believed, then removing sulphur in the fuel will reduce the ozone-destroying impact of supersonic transport.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290">
        <a href="#cite_note-290">
         [284]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Concorde's technical leap forward boosted the public's understanding of conflicts between technology and the environment as well as awareness of the complex decision analysis processes that surround such conflicts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291">
        <a href="#cite_note-291">
         [285]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In France, the use of
       <a href="/wiki/Noise_barrier" title="Noise barrier">
        acoustic fencing
       </a>
       alongside
       <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">
        TGV
       </a>
       tracks might not have been achieved without the 1970s controversy over aircraft noise.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292">
        <a href="#cite_note-292">
         [286]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the UK, the
       <a href="/wiki/Campaign_to_Protect_Rural_England" title="Campaign to Protect Rural England">
        CPRE
       </a>
       has issued
       <a href="/wiki/Tranquillity#Mapping_tranquillity" title="Tranquillity">
        tranquillity maps
       </a>
       since 1990.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293">
        <a href="#cite_note-293">
         [287]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Some sources say Concorde typically flew 17 miles per U.S. gallon (14 L/100 km; 20 mpg
       <sub>
        ‑imp
       </sub>
       ) per passenger.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294">
        <a href="#cite_note-294">
         [288]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_perception">
        Public perception
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Public perception">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ConcordeBG.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="284" data-file-width="600" height="104" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/ConcordeBG.jpg/220px-ConcordeBG.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/ConcordeBG.jpg/330px-ConcordeBG.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/ConcordeBG.jpg/440px-ConcordeBG.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ConcordeBG.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Parade flight at Queen's
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Jubilee_of_Elizabeth_II" title="Golden Jubilee of Elizabeth II">
          Golden Jubilee
         </a>
         in June 2002
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Concorde was normally perceived as a privilege of the rich, but special circular or one-way (with return by other flight or ship) charter flights were arranged to bring a trip within the means of moderately well-off enthusiasts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295">
        <a href="#cite_note-295">
         [289]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The aircraft was usually referred to by the British as simply "Concorde".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296">
        <a href="#cite_note-296">
         [290]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In France it was known as "le Concorde" due to "le", the definite article,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OxLangFrGlos_297-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-OxLangFrGlos-297">
         [291]
        </a>
       </sup>
       used in
       <a href="/wiki/French_grammar" title="French grammar">
        French grammar
       </a>
       to introduce the name of a ship or aircraft,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298">
        <a href="#cite_note-298">
         [292]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the capital being used to distinguish a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proper_name" title="Proper name">
        proper name
       </a>
       from a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_noun" title="Common noun">
        common noun
       </a>
       of the same spelling.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OxLangFrGlos_297-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-OxLangFrGlos-297">
         [291]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-299">
        <a href="#cite_note-299">
         [293]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In French, the common noun
       <i>
        concorde
       </i>
       means "agreement, harmony, or peace".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301">
        <a href="#cite_note-301">
         [N 7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Concorde's pilots and British Airways in official publications often refer to Concorde both in the singular and plural as "she" or "her".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302">
        <a href="#cite_note-302">
         [295]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303">
        <a href="#cite_note-303">
         [N 8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As a symbol of national pride, an example from the BA fleet made occasional
       <a href="/wiki/Flypast" title="Flypast">
        flypasts
       </a>
       at selected Royal events, major air shows and other special occasions, sometimes in formation with the
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Arrows" title="Red Arrows">
        Red Arrows
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304">
        <a href="#cite_note-304">
         [296]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On the final day of commercial service, public interest was so great that grandstands were erected at Heathrow Airport. Significant numbers of people attended the final landings; the event received widespread media coverage.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305">
        <a href="#cite_note-305">
         [297]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2006, 37 years after its first test flight, Concorde was announced the winner of the Great British Design Quest organised by the BBC and the
       <a href="/wiki/Design_Museum" title="Design Museum">
        Design Museum
       </a>
       . A total of 212,000 votes were cast with Concorde beating other British design icons such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Mini" title="Mini">
        Mini
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mini_skirt" title="Mini skirt">
        mini skirt
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_E-Type" title="Jaguar E-Type">
        Jaguar E-Type
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tube_map" title="Tube map">
        Tube map
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">
        World Wide Web
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Red_telephone_box" title="Red telephone box">
        K2 telephone box
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Supermarine_Spitfire" title="Supermarine Spitfire">
        Supermarine Spitfire
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Concorde_beats_306-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Concorde_beats-306">
         [298]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307">
        <a href="#cite_note-307">
         [299]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Special_missions">
        Special missions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Special missions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px">
        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Queen_Elizabeth_II_and_Prince_Philip_disembark_from_a_British_Airways_Concorde.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="1902" data-file-width="2926" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Queen_Elizabeth_II_and_Prince_Philip_disembark_from_a_British_Airways_Concorde.jpg/220px-Queen_Elizabeth_II_and_Prince_Philip_disembark_from_a_British_Airways_Concorde.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Queen_Elizabeth_II_and_Prince_Philip_disembark_from_a_British_Airways_Concorde.jpg/330px-Queen_Elizabeth_II_and_Prince_Philip_disembark_from_a_British_Airways_Concorde.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Queen_Elizabeth_II_and_Prince_Philip_disembark_from_a_British_Airways_Concorde.jpg/440px-Queen_Elizabeth_II_and_Prince_Philip_disembark_from_a_British_Airways_Concorde.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">
           The Queen
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip,_Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh">
           The Duke of Edinburgh
          </a>
          disembark Concorde in 1991.
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The heads of France and the United Kingdom flew Concorde many times.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308">
        <a href="#cite_note-308">
         [300]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Presidents
       <a href="/wiki/Georges_Pompidou" title="Georges Pompidou">
        Georges Pompidou
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309">
        <a href="#cite_note-309">
         [301]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Val%C3%A9ry_Giscard_d%27Estaing" title="Valéry Giscard d'Estaing">
        Valéry Giscard d'Estaing
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310">
        <a href="#cite_note-310">
         [302]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Mitterrand" title="François Mitterrand">
        François Mitterrand
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311">
        <a href="#cite_note-311">
         [303]
        </a>
       </sup>
       regularly used Concorde as French flagman aircraft in foreign visits. Queen
       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">
        Elizabeth II
       </a>
       and Prime Ministers
       <a href="/wiki/Edward_Heath" title="Edward Heath">
        Edward Heath
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jim_Callaghan" title="Jim Callaghan">
        Jim Callaghan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">
        Margaret Thatcher
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/John_Major" title="John Major">
        John Major
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">
        Tony Blair
       </a>
       took Concorde in some charter flights such as the Queen's trips to Barbados on her Silver Jubilee in 1977, in 1987 and in 2003, to the Middle East in 1984 and to the United States in 1991.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-burleigh2008_312-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-burleigh2008-312">
         [304]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">
        Pope John Paul II
       </a>
       flew on Concorde in May 1989.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313">
        <a href="#cite_note-313">
         [305]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Concorde sometimes made special flights for demonstrations, air shows (such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Farnborough_Airshow" title="Farnborough Airshow">
        Farnborough
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Paris_Air_Show" title="Paris Air Show">
        Paris-LeBourget
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MAKS_(air_show)" title="MAKS (air show)">
        MAKS
       </a>
       air shows) as well as parades and celebrations (for example, of Zürich airport's anniversary in 1998). The aircraft were also used for private charters (including by the President of
       <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">
        Zaire
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Mobutu_Sese_Seko" title="Mobutu Sese Seko">
        Mobutu Sese Seko
       </a>
       on multiple occasions), for advertising companies (including for the firm
       <a href="/wiki/Oki_Electric_Industry" title="Oki Electric Industry">
        OKI
       </a>
       ), for Olympic torch relays (
       <a href="/wiki/1992_Winter_Olympics" title="1992 Winter Olympics">
        1992 Winter Olympics in Albertville
       </a>
       ) and for observing
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse" title="Solar eclipse">
        solar eclipses
       </a>
       , including the
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse_of_June_30,_1973" title="Solar eclipse of June 30, 1973">
        solar eclipse of June 30, 1973
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time.com_314-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-time.com-314">
         [306]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spirit_315-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-spirit-315">
         [307]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and again for the
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse_of_August_11,_1999" title="Solar eclipse of August 11, 1999">
        total solar eclipse on August 11, 1999
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316">
        <a href="#cite_note-316">
         [308]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317">
        <a href="#cite_note-317">
         [309]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Records">
        Records
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Records">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The fastest transatlantic airliner flight was from New York JFK to London Heathrow on 7 February 1996 by the British Airways G-BOAD in 2 hours, 52 minutes, 59 seconds from take-off to touchdown aided by a 175 mph (282 km/h) tailwind.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SST_makes_record_flight_318-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-SST_makes_record_flight-318">
         [310]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 13 February 1985, a Concorde charter flight flew from London Heathrow to
       <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Airport" title="Sydney Airport">
        Sydney
       </a>
       —on the opposite side of the world—in a time of 17 hours, 3 minutes and 45 seconds, including refuelling stops.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319">
        <a href="#cite_note-319">
         [311]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-320">
        <a href="#cite_note-320">
         [312]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321">
        <a href="#cite_note-321">
         [313]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Concorde also set other records, including the official
       <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_A%C3%A9ronautique_Internationale" title="Fédération Aéronautique Internationale">
        FAI
       </a>
       "Westbound Around the World" and "Eastbound Around the World" world air speed records.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-322">
        <a href="#cite_note-322">
         [314]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 12–13 October 1992, in commemoration of the 500th anniversary of Columbus’ first New World landing, Concorde Spirit Tours (US) chartered Air France Concorde F-BTSD and
       <a href="/wiki/Circumnavigation" title="Circumnavigation">
        circumnavigated
       </a>
       the world in 32 hours 49 minutes and 3 seconds, from
       <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">
        Lisbon
       </a>
       , Portugal, including six refuelling stops at
       <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">
        Santo Domingo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">
        Acapulco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Honolulu" title="Honolulu">
        Honolulu
       </a>
       , Guam,
       <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">
        Bangkok
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">
        Bahrain
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-323">
        <a href="#cite_note-323">
         [315]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The eastbound record was set by the same Air France Concorde (F-BTSD) under charter to Concorde Spirit Tours
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spirit_315-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-spirit-315">
         [307]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in the US on 15–16 August 1995. This promotional flight circumnavigated the world from New York/JFK International Airport in 31 hours 27 minutes 49 seconds, including six refuelling stops at
       <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">
        Toulouse
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">
        Dubai
       </a>
       , Bangkok, Andersen AFB in
       <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">
        Guam
       </a>
       , Honolulu, and
       <a href="/wiki/Acapulco" title="Acapulco">
        Acapulco
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-324">
        <a href="#cite_note-324">
         [316]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By its 30th flight anniversary on 2 March 1999 Concorde had clocked up 920,000 flight hours, with more than 600,000 supersonic, many more than all of the other supersonic aircraft in the Western world combined.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325">
        <a href="#cite_note-325">
         [317]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On its way to the
       <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Flight" title="Museum of Flight">
        Museum of Flight
       </a>
       in November 2003, G-BOAG set a New York City-to-Seattle speed record of 3 hours, 55 minutes, and 12 seconds.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-326">
        <a href="#cite_note-326">
         [318]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Due to the restrictions on supersonic overflights within the USA the flight was granted permission by the Canadian authorities for the majority of the journey to be flown supersonically over sparsely-populated Canadian territory.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Specifications">
        Specifications
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Concorde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Specifications">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="floatright">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Concordev1.0.png" title="Other line drawings of Concorde">
        <img alt="Other line drawings of Concorde" data-file-height="1297" data-file-width="2004" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Concordev1.0.png/400px-Concordev1.0.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Concordev1.0.png/600px-Concordev1.0.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Concordev1.0.png/800px-Concordev1.0.png 2x" width="400"/>
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Concorde_G-BOAC.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="352" data-file-width="1800" height="43" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Concorde_G-BOAC.png/220px-Concorde_G-BOAC.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Concorde_G-BOAC.png/330px-Concorde_G-BOAC.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Concorde_G-BOAC.png/440px-Concorde_G-BOAC.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Concorde_G-BOAC.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Concorde G-BOAC
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p style="font-size: 90%; margin:0; padding: .2em">
       <i>
        Data from
       </i>
       <i>
        The Wall Street Journal
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fliengi_204-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-fliengi-204">
         [199]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        The Concorde Story
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKelly200552_327-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKelly200552-327">
         [319]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        The International Directory of Civil Aircraft
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrawley200314_74-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrawley200314-74">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <span style="font-size: 120%;">
        <b>
         General characteristics
        </b>
       </span>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <b>
         Crew:
        </b>
        3 (2 pilots and 1
        <a href="/wiki/Flight_engineer" title="Flight engineer">
         flight engineer
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Capacity:
        </b>
        92–120 passengers
        <br/>
        (128 in high-density layout)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328">
         <a href="#cite_note-328">
          [N 9]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Length:
        </b>
        202 ft 4 in (61.66 m)
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <a href="/wiki/Wingspan" title="Wingspan">
          Wingspan
         </a>
         :
        </b>
        84 ft 0 in (25.6 m)
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Height:
        </b>
        40 ft 0 in (12.2 m)
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Fuselage internal length:
        </b>
        129 ft 0 in (39.32 m)
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Fuselage width:
        </b>
        maximum of 9 ft 5 in (2.87 m) external 8 ft 7 in (2.62 m) internal
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Fuselage height:
        </b>
        maximum of 10 ft 10 in (3.30 m) external 6 ft 5 in (1.96 m) internal)
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Wing area:
        </b>
        3,856 ft
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        (358.25 m
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <a href="/wiki/Manufacturer%27s_empty_weight" title="Manufacturer's empty weight">
          Empty weight
         </a>
         :
        </b>
        173,500 lb (78,700 kg)
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Useful load:
        </b>
        245,000 lb (111,130 kg)
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Maximum fuel load:
        </b>
        210,940 lb (95,680 kg)
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Maximum taxiing weight:
        </b>
        412,000 lb (187,000 kg)
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_engine" title="Aircraft engine">
          Powerplant
         </a>
         :
        </b>
        4 ×
        <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce/Snecma_Olympus_593" title="Rolls-Royce/Snecma Olympus 593">
         Rolls-Royce/Snecma Olympus 593
        </a>
        Mk 610 Afterburning
        <a href="/wiki/Turbojet" title="Turbojet">
         turbojets
        </a>
        <ul>
         <li>
          <b>
           Dry thrust:
          </b>
          32,000
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pound-force" title="Pound-force">
           lbf
          </a>
          (140 kN) each
         </li>
         <li>
          <b>
           Thrust with
           <a href="/wiki/Afterburner" title="Afterburner">
            afterburner
           </a>
           :
          </b>
          38,050 lbf (169 kN) each
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       <span style="font-size: 120%;">
        <b>
         Performance
        </b>
       </span>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <b>
         <a href="/wiki/V_speeds#Regulatory_V-speeds" title="V speeds">
          Maximum speed
         </a>
         :
        </b>
        <a href="/wiki/Mach_number" title="Mach number">
         Mach
        </a>
        2.04 (≈1,354 mph, 2,179 km/h, 1,176 knots) at cruise altitude
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <a href="/wiki/V_speeds#Vc" title="V speeds">
          Cruise speed
         </a>
         :
        </b>
        Mach 2.02 (≈1,340 mph, 2,158 km/h, 1,164 knots) at cruise altitude
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <a href="/wiki/Range_(aeronautics)" title="Range (aeronautics)">
          Range
         </a>
         :
        </b>
        3,900 nmi (4,488.04 mi, 7,222.8 km)
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <a href="/wiki/Ceiling_(aeronautics)" title="Ceiling (aeronautics)">
          Service ceiling
         </a>
         :
        </b>
        60,000 ft (18,300 m)
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <a href="/wiki/Rate_of_climb" title="Rate of climb">
          Rate of climb
         </a>
         :
        </b>
        10,000 ft/min
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-329">
         <a href="#cite_note-329">
          [320]
         </a>
        </sup>
        (50.80 m/s)
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <a href="/wiki/Lift-to-drag_ratio" title="Lift-to-drag ratio">
          lift-to-drag
         </a>
         :
        </b>
        <i>
         Low speed–
        </i>
        3.94,
        <i>
         Approach–
        </i>
        4.35,
        <i>
         250 kn, 10,000 ft–
        </i>
        9.27,
        <i>
         Mach 0.94–
        </i>
        11.47,
        <i>
         Mach 2.04–
        </i>
        7.14
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <a href="/wiki/Fuel_efficiency" title="Fuel efficiency">
          Fuel consumption
         </a>
         :
        </b>
        46.85 lb/mi (13.2 kg/km) operating for maximum range
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <a href="/wiki/Thrust-to-weight_ratio" title="Thrust-to-weight ratio">
          Thrust/weight
         </a>
         :
        </b>
        0.373
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Maximum
         <a href="/wiki/Heat_shield" title="Heat shield">
          nose tip temperature
         </a>
         :
        </b>
        260 °F (130 °C)
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">
          Runway
         </a>
         requirement
        </b>
        (with maximum load): 3,600 m (11,800 ft)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-330">
         <a href="#cite_note-330">
          [321]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>

          </span>

           </a>

           <a href="/wiki/Messerschmitt_Me_262" title="Messerschmitt Me 262">

           </a>
           .
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-29">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           This apparently took place some time in 1957, according to Conway's unclear statement about "the following year" which apparently references the first STAC meeting in late 1956.
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-124">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

          <span class="reference-text">
           "It is the world's most efficient jet engine." -Ricky Bastin, Concorde Engineer
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nova_72-3">

             [68]
            </a>

          </span>

          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           Quote: "Airbus, the manufacturer of Concorde, has said it is becoming uneconomic to maintain the ageing craft and that it will no longer provide spare parts for it."
          </span>

          <span class="reference-text">
